Monday's Consolidation


Audience data platform Brilig has been acquired by CRM agency Merkle. Terms were not announced. Ad tech consolidation continues to propel forward as "early" players (AdExchanger "ripple dissolve": See Brilig's 2009 Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qA5AtHfDUwCypvNxlLhfRGLpHVwU5b-p21BfdAqd5QW0__Bk3uBS-YHC-gEqOJAqV73_SCKAj4LpUzYjqUykhPyxooicwg1Lf809Xg07f91I0Ve3zKJQ55pAhCVrJItPVgP11niseGBiuWHCZ04O0jBxFkCv_7XKD-Dj_TpB61avNFVv4PacVcGGdLaSGR__Ny20hti9vE3euIR6vnSmUiorjPWx0wePLAq_goQy7XiqAbeXM4EJS0X1XWETdSas> &A) who were a part of the demand-side platform world craze either grow larger and sustainable on their own - or are quietly gobbled up by larger platform players who at the very least may be looking to "acquihire." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qA5AtHfDUwDAQsFqxG193e5FxcdWRTvctlv5nO6xfRolUdNBIpJH7rwEQQeoCeu7D26HdX36Dh53GZhhAB3AK3E0ABvAjVE9vM2I3gtEYYuXj3Rr5BeK5P3_LkV4-eKOVu_v7oNYFfxxdApVYTkVKJb2KP1z0qy-oB_BkmPOtzTfuC49nlpBoBg3G7WYDROMNrlMb3nc6O6YpMeywoja-PNcC5vmpIFl8BauRbRnraxe9WrhBr_m2A==> . Merkle EVP and CMO Craig Dempster noted his company's acquisitive predilections in the release: "The addition of Brilig (data), 5th Finger (mobile), Social Amp (social), IMPAQT (search) and IMPAQT Trading (media) enhances our established online and offline marketing assets." 


Auction And The Agency


The agency of record is being dragged into the world of e-auctions according to Ad Age's Alexandra Bruell. Procurement's steely hand is at work as they look to drive down agency prices on behalf of the marketer (maybe). There's nuance to the auction, too, as Bruell writes, "Depending on the model, agencies might be able to see only how they're ranked on a scale of the highest and lowest bids. In other cases, they might be able to view all competing bids. The results provide the client with a way to benchmark the cost of different agencies. In some cases only the lowest bidders can win the business or make it to the next round." There's more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qA5AtHfDUwDI8uiPF00MxzdAMVekh2tZojG6PwJ5ddrTADc9ZpCkkfre4CEdPAVJE-CPMSLaK6ZxPABbGELvwWfriMvXZC1H_j5unZLHqqLDhXa8ImeAkdG4QRvKXhtrgtkG2GIzI3XkA8eolMe6yT1wQR2J6LYWHWxjtwzqsPZhwrDzgXFtzaH-GTNH8EcGj1VCNrDf1uE=>  


When Tags Collide


On the Evidon blog, CEO Scott Meyer announced a new product called "Evidon Encompass Revenue Protection" - part of its suite of "website control platform" solutions. Meyer explains, "The new Revenue Protection module, which clients will have free access to through the end of the year, brings new value-gaining unprecedented insight into 'the redirect chain' to see how all trackers are getting onto your site. When you know, you can start to create business rules that stop problems before they start." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qA5AtHfDUwASnpRJa5vuoSQ6OKsR3-UmvTtWLHCynCG79jLpNcQr2-UA23i6RFJunBZ41A96WxK5H1BBA1B4svQFsY3gtKybW3Tj3OteSDrP1jQ7la2PuqKDTpa7rOJHKpWKVhq-IEwLLJLhbcNvJgCDlcYk248qaGqje6dOYgrPOvBCa28A4LNG76V2MB1swR-URqZxRAQ=>  Evidon appears to be getting increasingly into the tag management business that companies like Krux, BrightTag, Tagman and Ensighten are already slicing and dicing to differing degrees. 


Amazon Opt-Out


Even as Amazon works slowly to build out its own advertising capabilities, the e-tailer will let Kindle Fire users pay a $15 fee to opt out of ads, the WSJ's Greg Bensinger reported. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qA5AtHfDUwDQZgCW8O7U8LXwC8nzrLTMtbu8japw6ZSHTcqgvhpLcIlWdwMuvSTz_4uTQUHcnlE781m7GA4vugV3f4dk1qiNQGVnRY9JvDpDG9Qtotnm1Sg7igxPXFt5jXW2Ue4hje9WVIYOm43teJQxVjfFoPXyI5HBU7-3i6ioA4REO7WTZ1rwCMe458ej> . "We know from our Kindle reader line that customers love our special offers and very few people choose to opt out," Amazon said in a statement. "We're happy to offer customers the choice." 

Scoring Brands


Can facebook fan data disrupt an old, marketing stalwart? "Too soon to tell" says the AdExchanger Magic 8 ball. But, brand rankings like those provided annually by companies like Interbrand may need to get more real-time. Social ad company Optim.al provides its version of brand rankings for August and reports that Coca-Cola, Reese's, Monster Energy, Pepsi, Cover Girl, NFL, Coupon Cabin, Aeropostale, Cheez-It and Hollister Co are on the rise. (Suddenly) see more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qA5AtHfDUwCyf0lpYv3IwuRsWpZypRWD9lk_wsgNLPE_13D4N-lt_rw3B8kVe55tYBbU5yQ112ysiJoP2np4sYYnjHKb_o5YB1sX-C-J1JNLondwf0awMaF5LSKHAVByehbhG3FRegNEnbWKIV_q4A==>  


So Long, adCenter


Microsoft is tweaking the nomenclature for its search ad products. Let it be known: adCenter will henceforth be called Bing Ads, while the search network encompassing Bing, Yahoo and some partner sites has been re-christened Yahoo! Bing Network. Read a blog post.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qA5AtHfDUwDJxFQbcprYKMXqEcDC3g3Y0zalxurAdXPVUniTfvb9vaRbK806WJE5j-UZMaT6yTMrvO8YPaz4mb5Ev1TI2hFQtRBSj7VDcYV3WekA8mpuLnyTnc83LEHcdqlBqsljWJwlI_QdDL7aVcYWiThOxNoSOU6KhJMU68Q58QiXIELvOUBeVGKBTHEzzY3rqQTzSCdBCNxfd_dYbZaG-li6lyzkrMSrt2YgGD13lVT4-mf2UajtWXV5WWaZZztB5gStgvo=> 


Improving on the DMA


Designated Market Areas are getting a run for their money, as local media researcher Borrell Associates proposes a more granular array of DMRs (Digital Marketing Regions). As ClickZ's Kate Kaye notes, regional ad sellers would be the beneficiaries: "Most local media outlets can reach 28 percent share of their DMAs at the most, with many hitting only in the single digits, said Borrell Associates CEO Gordon Borrell. But that can change drastically when looking at the more hyper-local DMRs." Read more and see the map.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qA5AtHfDUwB4ErSLZeuaiYHCYjZRFiuOksv7dzXcsCUqGkTBj_MlBf2pJN6QSh7UNCSIQF0RDD94o0wO4j8VYWmU3Ei4AMXFLvr60hTvQNRkf9TPU_EcS3SJ5tSZG5-1PxrKbAkMfLA76SXiFuve6TmH2m6-L6q7OHFCS7a6eb7WcgmrEEZA0CzfpcktwJkOfJH1egfbQzJ3Xcd0cVuGkP7DIUR2v35ktJSQmMRGmyNRPWw1uoF0pO1VI0Mr4dpU4j6JqjmZ_SxF6fWTsTVM2JQObKHPJwURK9kEP1AuUQHEfcbhMIS2EpPhziUWLkJxQyv40N5Zt88YW_4MApt9kHIfpvL4vBy3NJqwIWZhW-Q=> 


Testing Targeting's Efficacy


The "ad effectiveness" lawsuit brought <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qA5AtHfDUwAXaCFe4WaCgrEsM0QAmj7JcyOLDTAMryXpGqtb85cyupsdKBLedqdfnWRGyObe8DYnjw6oAl__NVvd7_W_yn06htsGm_XoXlNTAxHfA051itxRkVxwe8Cc0IP24ACPAOaAvcKMP45KrrYZnF4LkCMYkVLvdYuIJatz4hhkYGep2w==>  by comScore in May isn't slowing one of the DoubleVerify, one of the defendants in the case, down. The company has spent the past 10 months working with WPP analytics provider Kantar Media Compete on determining how well ad targeting actually works. "The big difference is that the entire basis for our measurement is based down to the user," said Mark Pearlstein, DoubleVerify svp of sales and marketing, telling Adweek's Tim Peterson that it represents a "building-block level" for digital marketers. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qA5AtHfDUwCupW5pdSe02xxfjWWLmnIAJIxd2oTs1-mkOdbYUtQUTGFbEVNDGZi7WbWK5YLPIEm-p8FkQiPFYSBXw_6CbSjEd-4lV-JDyjZcC5y6-MMd1c5fg-TXL9xlrpRYYxRgs9sZh4Rp67cK7_h_J_Cg-f5VABxH0oPFQf2FpHq6GtV_X9skJmkXpA35> . And, here's the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001qA5AtHfDUwA-u2CnE_fgefkwSwsYbHM5CNKRu5fkGjSFgjkhyqoxgGDLUF2VxRBHV9UncUndO0SGGHVibLarXnXWEKgVzgr5KoG0yWFyGKJfNkLt6hQ3hyBOmv0Eb2TCV8j8ckhG8p6k0nSzKU4eCTN-395TZEs1nPxB61Sagjg=> .


Web Stats


Citi analyst Mark Mahaney remarks on the comScore traffic stats just released to clients for August, "Unique Visitors to Facebook declined 6% Y/Y in August, down 5 pts from July's 1% Y/Y decline. This marks the first material decline in traffic to FB that we've seen to-date, a negative trend in our opinion."

Pub-Side Consolidation


AudienceFuel has been acquired by Clever On Demand says TechCrunch's Anthony Ha who adds that Active International has made another investment in the combined companies to be known as AudienceFuel. Is Active looking for a digital version of barter? Clever on Demand CEO Troy McConnell tells Ha "the two teams are working to integrate their services. (...) Clever On Demand by filling inventory with ads from multiple networks, AudienceFuel by allowing publishers to exchange inventory with each other (as illustrated in the diagram below)." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKa8BalETF0Zqd7z3gz2u5JL2x7Qlndd0iLwfHBirKNmmYBkgbKB8nYOeArxk9DGA0a_MZA1RNxGrD6T9gzYstj6lYlGkI8HYhVFtQkMLnDqhFkWRV1t3h-uT_bz2wt_SKaP69GqhMSSfnnmaz7GBLZbLHJc79d5UBvXPYref9J27az8Q_WDe2xv> . And, see the new AudienceFuel exec team. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKa1_9CepmneuDdJBz--yNpnfjuA92pWRPi2GS9ZoIsnAfwiapROPI3n9i3HHapsxRb4KbOnX2dvjPb6s91Gr1EDfEiaMadDXThQDDGz2UJzaFsXX8jNZiOqsNHbnKJqm89UTIr8Dh-J29a6OQYMaOt-unU5A-MJ51w=>  


eBay's Data U-Turn?


On ExchangeWire, Phuong Nguyen, Head of Advertising UK at eBay, discusses a new partnership with Rubicon Project to provide what he claims is the "UK's largest private ad exchange." He adds that the exchange has a reach of 17 million monthly unique users, up to five billion impressions and the "data insights from shopper-ready consumers." As you may recall, eBay pulled its intent data out of data exchanges in 2011 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKYHyvuhNK8JpOUkXQTmPeCuJe_t3LQuRDAe94ZN_LGBVEhx-Y7edHVVawx88IPHydZBRa4EYatB-pdNRUHSF1Jj1FTOE3TKRjLmNLUhA4WNVH_nVjwgSuxuq1Sxv06epC619mSiEY0L5w==> . It appears the intent data may be "back" in a private exchange model. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKaioybLIoRXnvkZ2jfDtK4VBrgCTqhIGnKb6J-iugvYW5Tgf0Hu0kNukaKWFKKgnNymkvsk61hJEY6zt1qM-NW6U8U3fqUTqoYEDayrf0VBKiLOAXczrsqcVxGHZ0MOy3A02OZ1GNTd6u2NDWkDNzY1SyLLJ8TYar7ROqFmNZwI8KX0piEovnUsaeL1x8_-0S9HRU3u-KfFHyRF1qmpdR8fHTCRACePcKM3o1m1yNLhh2fnWLuUBtmw6Y_pbJ9OV5WROmgZRKd0irSUvzpNVV8GmBy90Owz6FrOB5kmIGQQHHlFL2U5lJhVMYSZxBva3NrE-ivEe9vMJA==>  And - how about this piece on Wired <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKYFHyJqGaFXwNcLJB8gGDiHJFViM1RMFWf-Ui0PlTMSH5aEK8BXmKMRs2UTQ5SkgIlbehEJTXzQ-VcYLIKRzqZptpAUH2_EA6bo76np0TKzOFQXAWlV6QPn5h1yCwp-sNO7r9q8qCFLZt2uHBuW7GimEgzf8HukVvc=>  about Ebay's acquisition of 6-person Svpply - retargeting for all products everywhere? Imagine the datasets. 


The Ad Data Wave


Data-driven, digital, audience buying gets a tip of the cap in a "big data"-meets-tech piece by The New York Times' Steve Lohr. He writes, "Rocket Fuel [CEO George] John says [he] is using some of the ideas he worked on in the 1990s as a doctoral student focusing on artificial intelligence at Stanford - research that was supported with government dollars from the National Science Foundation <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKahr7FHqryHpmstorzj53G0IkaVsRIgoepqR64auGybPjC25dyqZKOBsQeilxjeQf5qqsOZltCZF6FMBmCmc01sNzPg9gf2xK4=>  and other agencies, as is so often the case. In the last few years, building a business around those ideas has become achievable and affordable. 'And a lot of it has to do with the underlying technology,' Mr. John says." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKZyuyoNj6Yk7vOgyK6k8eoZmKpHuoAGxUJzUVGFHesn4004g05e_Z_x_L1HmYm6HXXST4E5pwOxRzLUgHiPte05g_RARMNW3m4trhrvkacM6ELONt83YZJ9Nx57mfZeHTwHEGV5u0BIXs8VN922kReyrQX-l4_WiN4zkBnVrTU3OpfeAKArQWYKIuYllNf48Cu3GOlXS0MrEN6oTxDcaAJA>  


Butter or Parkay?


BlueKai CEO Omar Tawakol offers opinion on All Things D on whether it's better to have more data or a great algo. He wrItes, "If you have to choose, having more data does indeed trump a better algorithm. However, what is better than just having more data on its own is also having an algorithm that annotates the data with new linkages and statistics which alter the underlying data asset." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKbhJNmiKksLBVgNW_w_N7YSZgkcQbu4kVbfOfuldO_O6Pw7vasTnxekEA5eeXtLmjVEpDuFEIVWX81R5kz9Jf0e4q35Z9syzvYGjY82cG9C3GAsnKS9aWtR-hlxKr0i_ohSd2dVVEw7q8EHT1cv7dlvfldHL38CkcSiFopP5ughsGWCKbkq-RdD> . Tawakol wasn't done with opinion-making. Yesterday, he tweeted <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKZE8ebSzjnfD9TA-E1bbx-_5V4s4e3sKl550qDDTAeD7o9MwQqgQ08Zl8vr7UhSvRkpBUQsI1g4l7NXI0P0lft4tVcdK7FSHiT3qBcDbEGFzzJUWgR7w5ix3oYF5pUxKQsvRuedNw6VQ6YFlZMFIrSf> , "Targeting advertising = free content. If Amazon values ads at $15 per person on kindle. How much per person for all content owners?" 


Retargeting Freight Train


The ecommerce world is all hot and heavy about retargeting and the ability to hit bottom of the funnel intenders with an ad or two. Witness the reported success retargeter Mythings is enjoying in the U.S. MyThings managing director Michael Swope tells Internet Retailer that "his company has signed 60 U.S. merchants since it opened its first U.S. office in Scottsdale, AZ, nearly six months ago. 'Ten of the companies myThings has signed agreements with are in the Internet Retailer Top 500,"'says Swope, who adds that the company is on target to sign more than 100 U.S. merchants by the end of the year." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKbOAO6Eqa9G3-et0Z5dqDBJQ4-PJ2aUwweUUeLvoI4D3FVf7vhUgQOhkEa6e1QDIgs6ok-clwsNk-XHfpb4geREmWUNujdhAakpIrBFSSxiX-8ufQQHYQoYeX4FJJW8bZ7INDGMTMs06P6g5rZTJ123SgTXkD-2_FIpwtAGaXUU1vhlU-xaJjzx52O3vrOyXesSAlKXtlznlPRNBHoq45-b>  


First Look Fun


Is Google's Preferred Deals <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKZhIBfg0VnXqpr2kj4X2VtfHgJqW5aNbAoEJ6JVKHIiFYafYo-quBWx8vhUf1rYI7FMe-OfDZRJ06utWwdbEmVieA5lngcz39j8zdfxYmIQUO4CqE5QwLzCgQBE2636O6FPKNA6NxSyGJHTaAoxjr-uNXM2LAa9agBu_hYKzHe8mykMhsHxZJMzK3FKKPk2C6h7bTtJxHbhWw==>  having trouble gaining traction? Maybe. In an interview with AdMonsters' Gavin Dunaway, Google Senior Product Manager Drew Bradstock admits there have been challenges with the "first look at inventory" product and adds, "Both parties have had to be quite honest in terms of the volume of inventory publishers will offer, and also about how much of the available inventory a buyer will purchase. Once publishers and buyers began being open about their expectations, these deals started transacting very well. Ad Exchange's Preferred Deals offer system has really cut down on the time required to find new potential deals and on the effort required to get an offer live." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKZbpgxyIg3OVSVgrp77RIN8X4oVPyfJiEf6L1NvFJPRApY6ta4CEcFZPf0bLfghB4EmG8pdBqtgcE_0avJZZizg-GKebcvDXkjuTE7uPEWAB_MRtEl6NIe8A8h1s9LYynPiQzMu3sErPceI8wDk0WdI_3pDo_xHH-wG1LAu5-dFcg==>  This product was originally "Direct Deals" - read this Aug. 2011 interview with Google's Scott Spencer <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001A-07-ATTWKbWy94gv3xCjk1E0ERRPcu1FOvl7RVqT-tG7E1S7ms2oq2PC1mbUTw7kfLmFf0XcBDnGozLuGW9ZGr22Y6hoM-4L9GE8ZK4BSAUIgnpmqZrnxvDTo4v9jShvFyUHN74FJeGlgFhNyLUNH99Xx-ZYwtP88Wekd_Uw4jS_W_foadBjSrY6dtZ2TcnF1WGnMiafLWHi0Y5eB7ynLHOgd3irpeUdywn7-IM-4U-ecyCRZcewfkPNkKzi90C>  when he explained the product's features and offered a compare/contrast to a private exchange.

Tumbling Into Ads


AllThingsD's Liz Gannes reports that Tumblr, whose CEO has said not-nice things about advertising, has hired an ad man. Lee Brown, who hails from Groupon, will help sell big brands on native ad experiences. "Tumblr has experimented with brands like Adidas and Coke to create their own Tumblr blogs that are featured within the user dashboard - similar to how Twitter distributes advertising." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yaMB8g4ap1s6K5qPhNUEQ1jigW_g5NidPx405LLmVUDVHgTzHUa1XArFyVkxob2oWTEu-4lBq1bFr0ZcBz-Ot6OWRAQCrd0U-lSEZqgEwEw6lUykPjXqrVeUcvrPy-Rzd3iLPDULhFiIKd5TFTNBJG384ugE2r1EQoH4HDogMjOcqVxd7erco930Xxu0LcdeBcxx_9qBLirAeZjIG5E2SjKBfVZcmV5n>

Introducing Adobe Social, VP of Marketing Aseem Chandra tells TechCrunch's Anthony Ha,  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yaMB8g4ap1u0UkGZFF17SgAWt30mv9PLyuy6cInw_knDMkPMgHhayUK3RytDB65KMMOfqthayV2-yiH0ef86s9a2Ynb5SvJtCKP7ONT3aiSs3icdJkX_wmrnNqXxefB9E19y0z27zg7Yix99TpbrljovIRd1k2gECzz0WJL3_RenyY3R8IXvLOrqwrqcvq1CrRoqi3c94b5ug-g7VPD0PMVugtSGHIqPXCErvlVEZ7ShqGN7Ax216sjSu8otK_xh6NWmDTbnUdg-H41TNI0m868qsCo6ZL-q6D5gIX2YmQTbO1mFY_aQcA==> "[Marketers] have point solutions that solve specific problems, but they're not really connecting you back to the business issues." Twitter's Mobile Mojo


In a look at the mobile revenues of some big ad sellers, eMarketer homes in on the monetization race between Twitter and Facebook. Twitter wins, for now. "As users increasingly access Twitter via mobile devices, eMarketer believes that the tight integration between the company's ad products-particularly Promoted Tweets-and core user experience has made the subsequent shift toward diswplaying mobile advertisements relatively simple." Next year Facebook's mobile ad revenue will reach $387 million -- that's $113 million more than Twitter's. Both pale in comparison to Google. Ogle the charts.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yaMB8g4ap1t1OYAqHxSelA7woaqsZNGyqgCkrfQFUBImgG-Jrep-z4f4G6y0e1ZzjE1iZOIu8kbj9MfJewrJVL4o00vf5g84cHW52Yr6dAYIgMIvPuwlUph8n23pPh8k2Am6CLEP1U_17c09etEINu0Y1rJ5JzHr> 


The Algo Rules


Julia Angwin and Dana Mattioli look at the importance of the algorithm in pricing of today's consumer goods in The Wall Street Journal. Ecommerce platform provider Mercent is profiled: "[Mercent] changes the price of two million products an hour. Mercent says it makes price decision based on a variety of factors such as competitors' prices, competitors' shipping prices, manufacturer price restrictions and seasonal sales." Everything is becoming biddable. Read it (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yaMB8g4ap1tNjMsvnKI1g_eLPcr9OlXjiiTliffIrlfDq8VJWcLiQ8cbRoQjLSKCt7WSSXPjP-FXIfwsr881235MKAte6LOpIl60RE3mLbvk6gkCP1dNDz2BZFwsQaRuJNGeJFV8rCclVSjUFU02ckFC32DqS55VdlJfyBGAwGwH6VhSP1FggtUAlqbQTMLT> . 


Sellers And Q4


Upstream Group's Doug Weaver returns from his summer meditations with thoughts on Q4 and strategy for the itchy, twitchy digital seller. Weaver advises, "Shorten Your Stroke. Volume is not your friend right now. Rather than getting a lot of plates spinning all at once, make a conscious decision about which 4 or 5 accounts offer the biggest gettable yield." Read more from the maestro <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yaMB8g4ap1v7E5S5Fpfh9F3F54oX8tirIm8sX0ggRAK0mTcvMinA7lIJUFMkk9UJOKX7kz8fGGu4I0aGE8xdCoRcqLGIYr_PBlHDMvWfLzqgK6l6ebgHgfSAemc2d-pbkroKVkMY8CQ=> .

Prognostication


An investment column writer on Forbes claims the acquisition of ValueClick by Facebook is a good idea. Clem Chambers writes, "ValueClick demonstrably can do advertising. They monetise a broad range of what most people would class as 'low quality' inventory, the kind of inventory Facebook has. Facebook thinks it is 'high quality,' but the advertising jury who might buy it is still out." That would be an "interesting" merger of cultures. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001yaMB8g4ap1umCTCBL5g-FjgJEerCYHl8zD8zqS6txMVgKLumPzOnKhK29nZmeXLC9JPHUqOs1EmCB9w7eZ3rIJKP_2cSye8YUz6cxPf4Cq1iYJE8vxxfs_oHl8PkQvEI>

Display Ad-quisition


Rakuten LinkShare - you know, LinkShare - has acquired Utah-based display ad retargeter MediaForge. Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017AAx8NN6dKsaiD6VeGfI0PHuGQOI6xvoJY7njyPJEpHlPiydX5Xf1faonNkRqklRhzWaQwsWOAnjg9xl85FKmxB0BZp9iSYgVx7c6b6uwWNSJ0OQLIScIGDJuQZJAZzFnROzOVJ9pyUFNg7xQJEIV5rmRNgplMkIUWgZMTYYrlfXI6szgVzncr-r_o2yjkGrSd-FlwcocBR_yz-SehZjdg==>  The NextWeb points out, "The company, which was simply called LinkShare before it was acquired by Japanese e-commerce and Internet services giant Rakuten for $425 million <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017AAx8NN6dKujV5XNN_tno2nyCKKyL_S5HmdNaYwPOIsgZ7B0uOaPY6Zv-eHII56KDZoHi2iGBlzhBoAQ-CArryXb6MTtseIfL-dw50-2HXLZ6Rd_EZahq1APFMmqj4jGdyOceVrBGMA9zHdu5F-GLifwoqZnyr7UxIIZRo1dCYiAo7gkcR7Udfyyhov6J9-5cEpjpvEUcNQ=>  in cash back in 2005, says the deal will enable mediaFORGE to accelerate its expansion and reach throughout the US, Canada, the UK, and Japan." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017AAx8NN6dKvHauSMJFlVYLwGJZZO93zg2B18eFOYlMpzqQfbo77PJZweyFSe-FZwl6qKShvhpKphV8tePxGis4MjmVVHxckeLWqoWkRCq1AR70R8SdXfzu547ENY6uFO9HJz8Mt72mjwIx1WkJBr8nf3fInDjIt37VhOJc20CADLnAt7FmzxeqFBX7dj-2KHiK3FsXpWmKzq4p2GyAiYRcGh0R0WZEgsb-TjiYQRxaE=>  MediaForge's 50 employees will undoubtedly bring retargeting help to LinkShare Rakuten's affiliate business kinda like ValueClick is hoping Dotomi can fit with its Commission Junction unit. 


Google Everywhere


Google has teamed with market analysts Ipsos and Sterling Brands on a survey that's intended to quantify the amou <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017AAx8NN6dKujV5XNN_tno2nyCKKyL_S5HmdNaYwPOIsgZ7B0uOaPY6Zv-eHII56KDZoHi2iGBlzhBoAQ-CArryXb6MTtseIfL-dw50-2HXLZ6Rd_EZahq1APFMmqj4jGdyOceVrBGMA9zHdu5F-GLifwoqZnyr7UxIIZRo1dCYiAo7gkcR7Udfyyhov6J9-5cEpjpvEUcNQ=> nt of shuffling consumers do with their digital devices. Read the official blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017AAx8NN6dKsJkXQvyAvqKEBjuUDO8lIinZctyGQYpaMu6aFNRmjX8V1lU66E_0mrN2o6QIMIaRYxHR5QYyB8HJKxmj7zrUMVlxaK1Yh_7BcKqyzLu7yahj3yKtZfXfLZk4uQua_zDaIzCNZ-drvxTIDAWEZ02up27vCHsIkGYl5JVTAhg7M9GSMkU5mqAvSlOUEtEZ_NXjU=> . TechCrunch's Ingrid Lunden looks at the implications: "Given that Google will have advertising following users along the way, it also implies Google continuing to make sure that it has a role to play across all of the screens. Whether it does so as a software-only player, or also through an increasing role in the hardware itself, remains to be seen, although products like Google's new tablet with Asus, and its new ownership of Motorola Mobility, seem to point in the latter direction." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017AAx8NN6dKunUxGmEMv3ZWweJ-f6UIvatZGUrMsGR_SDGrOuX5qFsOVf-sd91Q4yWntE2kYQNSFzRZEfZ7VYIoHXOpHL7Gi4p7cPkybtlP28v2G3jxq-5UuSJ6oBZSWe2tzOrIEvRciaGUv1Koujfv-G2zg-plGPV0YGUWZmE9w0ZUEiJclOZ556xa8v4MQTu9CKnOU0p1lYPqdiraE79Jw86lWRcCSa> . 


FTC Eyes App Data 


Marketing mobile apps is becoming a bigger business. The FTC knows this and wants developer tactics to stay above-board. Data privacy is the keyword in a new set of Mobile App Marketing Principles from the agency, with bullet points like "Keep User Data Secure," "Collect Sensitive Information Only with Consent," and "Honor Your Privacy Promises." Download it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017AAx8NN6dKsiNJj3RsTQnrHbCSwO1hNQzNJKgnTqPjXTkguvMg67G-xGNHwinkrt-I7E2WJcLueigMvNJu7dN5UP7reYmdtDg-j0ZgoiWIbDcTUd15RCrh_oMNVAN32gfIEcmO0VKK_FakDV7j-q2iryEHi5YF-4EJgR71Cx4XI=>  


Real-Time Badders?


Rubicon-ers Jordan Mitchell and Neil Richter review the RTB marketplace in a piece on AdMonsters. The publisher side tech gurus claim to see nefarious buy side strategies. Here's one: "A bidding ring is when a group of bidders agree to not compete with each other in the same auction, and this is known to cause seller revenue problems within second price auctions. Single bid responses constrain market growth." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017AAx8NN6dKt5Cnm-Dmvdi4I6bMA9fPsinmnAZD4Medpk2XCkbw2naQqVxDA0KHBplgyc8TsL9R5r5Bvvtq__DA2pvEVIOYmJB0hP2YqNpqmS6ArbLp9vPofSboY0yWB2ic2dWtPnrm5RU9cwCanK3mjGHIHXB5b17xPxvJ9k3pGWOIuwEsZyJxQvmV_gosq5> . 


The Privacy Exchange


On Evidon's company blog, Turn SVP of Product Joshua Koran takes the controls and provides his overview of recent W3C's tracking protection working group machinations. He's concerned about the implications of Do-Not-Track if implemented. Koran writes, "While normalizing the web's approach to privacy could yield significant benefits to both consumers and businesses alike, there is an increasing risk that the standards being discussed could dramatically restrict the free flow of information that the W3C was originally intended to foster." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017AAx8NN6dKu-j5v93-gyAgxQbutH7txmAWRdWSW3YNW8cYhu3w8Thhaxz3uGhWGTxdOdZ4aboQKLdmnpvEQIhcWcsT7zaNb4A3XPAztDRdC2impIzA5uHUOi3akbTLv1Xc-TUJPI1t6Wqg6_7R9VoGZR4Pd5jeOOfAjsdX-ancYoV1BGn0l4uKv7C_0CP2Si4ccobm1mpqwhtNR0ycAXgw==>  


Viewability Everywhere


DoubleVerify inked a deal to bring its viewability data to Kantar Media Compete's panel-based research offering. According to MediaPost, "The agreement initially supports 'user-level' data and behavioral profiles, measuring reach, frequency and exposure. Then it will expand to focus more broadly." Read it.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017AAx8NN6dKvRJmiVxslYvUewBE_dUfvrUwQ6pRvK0HYSKQLKE3TKGMTuIqIOOFwTdcpCrqL-R_hT3Yl9q4HrCMpnDK4Ko7ZgtCrV8d-ECa5g3rxBxyiWVUI-JUg0qKaAj-ZRS-GY2L_r1m7rjrTiOrgKTyBmm2oBmAhorDzKOeRob_zkfl7HGFSmKj_H1v6ZP77YhTj9xpW7kI-iZVT77wDHSQdY4ShODPXBU3p8INs=> 


Feed Me Brands


Publisher yield optimization platform Maxifier announced it was going to become just a bit more brand friendly by virtue of a new partnership with Moat. According to the release, Maxifier will take a feed of Moat data which "will allow automated campaign optimization recommendations to be generated around this data, helping publishers ensure they deliver campaigns to an advertiser's branding metric." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017AAx8NN6dKtk1kGF5Aoi82j_xEVlizdZKmnVer5-hqnUglfKWWS_tmLuA5qp7mm5RfVbNm_4F4lpjzPIEKI5dfjZpprd1KFcXWXBTkVLCS1XkR0zE8eAJSQqLijZG_QmrSUIOii4q2Y_igAqnE0XMqKFPzrnKWh0WBY7bAe42HQleZ3H65kE73XkA1Xcat4hy78TWBmgTGVO0yjawNsNOQ==>

Twitter Flipped Off


Mike McCue, CEO of Social/mobile news reader Flipboard, discarded his seat on Twitter's board last month, but as a shareholder he still seems to care about the microblog's direction. In an interview with Telegraph UK's Katherine Rushton, his message is to go slow when it comes to chasing revenues. "Twitter was created as an open platform, an open communications ecosystem, and I hope it can stay that way," McCue says. "You have to be really careful not to let money get in the way of that." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0017AAx8NN6dKuqnxVsij14IouMwArbdNdWvTkQRo8_h7VMGCd-q2AZBt7tmAi0T1iWKhu4qzzzDcBXIVgL_NjuEd31Nl6tcC362SGNkxVngYV0gVxCFvF7wctZVV0c1Wp5hqr9J7hVAlS2eQ_Oy58-zArI_9t0qOuKuEzTehKyvpgdD_juguGvE0P1pIIBCfrlnnv0gmrI4ctULLKxPwxWv3u81m-hl8oSLQSm2Qdq8_J2bknejTw82NJD-XynOxR_U8dzB0rh_pU=> .

Targeting Email


Direct marketing agency Epsilon announced the launch of its Email Response Network (ERN). This baby can slice and dice your email data better than a Ginsu Knife <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001HeJDe0g60TjzqPfPoJDUjYtvh6IbZ2JsTQT03gFrA5LJuwjZpVb0HjWPSYZFfA7ZVovDIl3Zd-fllyE-NtRpU79aXwrVaoWWdk5XQjiyz484xI9GDKaBc2CFi_28fMOTyAC_5gYLkAChKv0ZPJZzEQ==> . From the release, the ERN "features Scheduling Intelligence, which allows email marketers to match the timing of deployment with each consumer's email interaction times. The optimal times are determined by the aggregation of data from both the marketer's list as well as the ERN's collective intelligence. The ERN builds a timing profile for every consumer on the client's list and calculates the optimal email interaction time for the individual consumer based on their email activity over a six month period." Target more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001HeJDe0g60TgXZ3l0rpzX__VWfqkRBqAUuMA7Ga21f_mLRY1sog85RoRpnFlx2MSGbymFd5dA7pBPmGjHa5kx3hSyJQRLbFjl9LLR9BEnFqZICm8q2xGbv4lJd8MXGLuxwOuWh6h2IO1RyTYZVakRniZtC73py1jSt25cHo6fB3RCzP3V8iCx-rzvuybNQZdcf4ba4JlZfb_aCetVn0ojhQ==> . 


Israeli Ad Tech


On Digiday, Jack Marshall profiles why there is a large number of Israelis active in advertising technology companies today. He talks to Taboola CEO Adam Singolda who offers a couple of reasons including, "The biggest factor is that everyone in the country serves at least three years in the military. The day-to-day work for us involved trying to solve problems with very little time, and almost absurdly limited resources. You're expected to solve mega problems with a very small staff, and with no ability to rely on third-party vendors. We had to invent a lot of stuff ourselves." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001HeJDe0g60TinC4U4QPmDc-HphkmpDMlTrMnMogm9S06d0eDbarhpDttEYdJzi8Tg0qDMVHY_Es6ub5J4_OH9DZqV-PwrdeEm2XzlynmK1RSvpmMJ2TAv0Zf1H-zp9J4EBl4LbmmQUddNdajSM10eygAUmPcXspPa-5KuhJbVIWQ=> 


Retargeting Momentum


Search retargeting platform Simpli.fi announced its 10,000th campaign, the hiring of a dozen people including the appointment of two VPs - all in one press release. CTO Paul Harrison is quoted on the campaign momentum, "Based on the acceleration, we expect to hit close to 20,000 campaigns by the end of 2012."
Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001HeJDe0g60TiUdCEB4Im3TDJyn-yOYbQBY667-96Qwg31itjU9-chqOnvnHhcvgEwPIXNWKfQJOIyAr2FOGHGqS16Ej921_MA4rOcsaMXb_U_27U6g12nTf-131qW7cXr8YP80tTdPi_IHWiWp07C2Eyr0O0qeCL3> . 


Publisher Exchange


France's La Place Media, which says it represents 80 sites from 12 premium publishers, has launched what it is positioning as a "premium" inventory exchange. Fabien Magalon, Managing Director, explains on ExchangeWire, "By combining truly premium publishers around one unique, visible proposition, La Place Media offers its publisher partners the ability to conquer a larger share of market than they would have by promoting their inventory individually. Scale drives demand." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001HeJDe0g60TguK5voBp_NVg15r9LUE0LEa9qnTK_2OjwWQN5kKrjOmowWxhmv2CnGZ7S2QqNzLW30A70mAOjZqlePE-Oo0CmTyLydGJP6CLthoEsbaagC7DjaX0EheEDt2vxFKyi8lc7n6LZk1W8ZfL7GCdb8Fcmb7kR9vg2EeccgsrS-dd6geoMkDaQfPn560ZFdnn4xXXvQqdKZxIJ0NmySxsiuaTKyfIcApkQU_6Y0zKEBx_1lbRGSk29GrlVMUUkn3CLvsTuzW7LxwavPnpRceI0xEUuBlcMik8dTFEM=> . Rubicon Project is providing the backbone according to Magalon. 


Facebook Upside


Facebook's name is not mud on Wall Street -- not entirely. In a research note covered by AllThingsD, JP Morgan's Doug Anmuth says "Facebook's ad strategy is working, and has lots of upside." Peter Kafka writes, "He's bumping his ad revenue estimates up, and thinks the mobile ads Mark Zuckerberg started selling this year will approach $1 billion by the end of 2013." Read it.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001HeJDe0g60TjiuQUAI80CrixP0xXs0pojXygslNLMc-4UixLWblL6dC9yjb7TmR7-M36SrnPvSMe8Sivv45ISBOmJM-uT345SvMg-rf5ktaoEdxzSlV1ikWrtRPyXDCT8olf37gfSURqi7RHk3NBVIYNQeEWZDx9W4gwy96REhD4kjpgtNLNzCvvMtlpt6TpS1MnIm7_FgA7RW9YpRdP3qXC6n7c75KS4mZFzh8YO09Y=> 


Learning From TV


Is it time for digital ad buyers and sellers to adopt contract guarantees, a la television? ESPN ad ops guy Rick Monihan says yes, arguing billing for contracted (not delivered) impressions would reduce friction. "Publishers and agencies alike face massive costs pursuing many small line item discrepancies. At the agency, costs are multiplied many times over by the number of sites they deal with." What about underdelivery, you say? He has answer for that too. Read it.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001HeJDe0g60ThEUlTdGAMhheCsB_6il-yRGy1b_c9HSCevaQeZoAe7Uw-68Af3o0u3ARblwzf-ogCWnbhoX-Zlp9odkeu0I0s5RYuRpGjueTi0_nRcqehJu3mrjvmR4mzRlpUERqI7rqztEPC65noim2Dlyq_asl_eW18o0-ZuS3J_bjWJpXI03dkokccDxjKzD9NKZ0H2TR0=> 


Facebook Stock Stuff


The Business Insider's Henry Blodgett looks at a new SEC filing <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001HeJDe0g60TgTJvKPDtKR_VeDl23lXtp4PHASyd7BRYZoaMTpaehCnhDlQUfCYhtqXWO1DyqU6d5iYG2RF1zbmtWXaFTNaGyL8tnyw3OSM047bghhVUjbXZfVhDDIbGbLzkTtu9vEvvMehPWDGGGLqekskxzwU8L8FQsJz9mYqaiwzX-eqtg0A6ysy3Ph__57ROuiE0ZFzd0=>  by Facebook and says that within its details is stock buyback at less than half of the company's original IPO price. He explains, "By deciding to withhold 101 million shares of the employee stock <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001HeJDe0g60Ti83K0PEes32GqMGC13ns64Znc485hjf-tG82ibr-zWkdaEkT8eEP_PYEwTG_4T14bjA-Fb8DNT670KpeZThlwixwsA5lGy3hgfk2T2r_j3NYGhthKGYu-FQSMxfnOigHgI--s4V7SdIS-B-TUgkXQfg90OYjvN2bo=>  grants and pay its tax-bill with cash on the balance sheet, Facebook is effectively buying back those shares and retiring them." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001HeJDe0g60ThJUr8ykek3FZy5AlY2hkiZ9wWmelAC5C_wsyN_FHK9Hak1F_v7b-cd36svc_9hEZ6YEnqoytgnGOym_GNjIsNBAm1YwoyzV5fkpORu6GWVoy_SjPAn74dGZDJCYe8tfEiYdnO1WKzB5fkU1W6QMnXu>  


Hunting With Data


With a simple turn of phrase, Magnetic CEO James Green turns the media buyer into a hunter in search of event-driven quarry in a think piece on Marketing Land. He highlights "effective times during the year for marketers to add data to their media plans" - and all in the name of his (and Magnetic's) favorite tactics, site and search retargeting. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001HeJDe0g60TiK4k2LtaxYx7ZEKHWEZPQVeIEfBdCFDUzSTuIDprDRCC3zd1su8sUrqjWUZJkP87mxBgS6srDdj9ayTvjkbjKHZs_FtLyIUIxI2VfzHquVTqk7tPjVRdqiFF9LiKlJcPtaSrdinPvBMG6sGFS2QHEczOBVnyY-A0LICsXS9Tu_fTKHSC3htOAxYVaPDinaETLGSdRVl8ARWwK5gOgG3LmJUmDSc7hSoEA=>  


Serving The Platforms


AdStaq CEO James Curran, a former product and biz dev lead for Lotame and a product manager for AOL's Advertising.com, is positioning his company as the ultimate platform connector. He sees other platforms as potential clients, not competitors and tells The Makegood's Tim Nichols: "We want to set up all those cool things for [platforms] that they think about in business development meetings, so they can focus on their products and how an integration may help their users... we'll never build a bidder for RTB, an ad server or a CRM solution. When a client needs one of these things, we bring them to the platforms." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001HeJDe0g60TgBAOryeAx6OThrvD5ywJkQZLxXS3SajY0Oh7YI0XO2t9HtPCY6t7xr_7OJ86Tz_LoDvkfBRUpQ1Dg9PxgIy78eXEY7b070Het6GxaQMhBD12ZGPr3TkHIw61fN66uQHkSq35CFsrGnKXQAOyhBhablT26K0CQbt4LR0_XBlRboS5iZtmWokSnhNYkdtRboISO6dWBW8xvYlAusdgl2JzPxtwGxIcyFExg=> .

Google Can't Unseat Nielsen


A Google TV Ads blog post explains that the company is abandoning its efforts to disrupt traditional buying models and will go after digital alone. Google's Shishir Mehrotra says, "We'll be doubling down on video solutions for our clients (like YouTube, AdWords for Video, and ad serving tools for web video publishers)." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OXsacGSihWnAxkWpkI6xd__myrOId0lqgNDVUYValghgUsHnrNcP4oNoddS9oiWUBYkvXhkUOGYEQXUiwL8eFLm6CVggJlp9M6SriH7SBJF4JHJukouj-VvPJl0ClPHNgcHDSlFHwHHrqsdGPrACYpWX6ntlPT1UwSjEdbTSi7EojbQcTt7XcQ==> . On ClickZ, Matt Kapko reads the tea leaves courtesty of industry expersts and says this means Google's battle to unseat Nielsen as a TV demo data "master" is over in spite of the valuable set-top box data which still remains unused. Read that one. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OXsacGSihWlmdrYQ0C3JK8ToGNtv_4-sUFYdDqenSp5caNwadkmNv7XJrPqKyHyo4Jg3oz9yOTF4C2nmf6RANyygjrI2C7pHlvAqCbl5u9e9l65ryBWqOZmgEXGXitcvA_Y1P-ppTPztK0nTjk07Xi4pYERmtKcL-0_bFY9P_OCJZQksIAKe_ShpjMtw6b0fNLjx_nYYrbjycM9fn_QnwvOlbSDHlhWe>  Dave Morgan, whose Simulmedia uses set top box data, tweeted <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OXsacGSihWmUWokUtsMHZyqSBIIJAH4RhtqkbA9K1Hx3T0mB6UlSWGXDZBfW6qnS_q6VYWewF2xjlH1u_HJxriALJ-5PO61ajGDnPCX20jPBhoiwjQxGZ43zQZUbA2MjSVByOBwbk4O3SYLiRf4zECa2eUF2Wc1gEkcNkLAMy9k=> , "Google TV Ads exit helps @Simulmedia & satellite ad sellers..." 


Connected TV


Speaking of Dave Morgan, he pitches Ad Age's readership -and Yahoo! - on the possibilities of selling a connected TV. He points to "what happened in China last week, when that country's largest internet company, Tencent, launched the Ice Screen, a branded multimedia TV set for the Chinese market." Morgan thinks this is where the consumer-electronics world may be headed. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OXsacGSihWksCFWcPBIwaSBNjNLaH0jDRN-16yvbtvlNAl1FfA6qsG0Vr_Q0uipl0-MqJ6qJmVd5Tvw1oWye4HZPlbMuAoFD_dd25eHydzwfgc5OJa7dTSt_u9uNS4785ui9pzljvYFzWwsXI1yEjugog0OEubORgyWYR90Xr8wna8md6FVi0W_fbCUO37VO>  


Policing Page "Like-age"


Late last Friday, a Facebook company blog post by "Facebook Security" said it was going to crack down on fake "Likes". So you better mean it the next time you click the "LIke" button or you could be going to Facebook Jail! Ok, maybe not. But, the post explains, "To be clear, we do not and have never permitted the purchase or sale of Facebook Likes as we only want people connecting to the Pages and brands with whom they have chosen to connect." Facebook expects this will delete less than 1% of page "like-age" from its system. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OXsacGSihWkfTBuYzEMst_SCaeLeLr51er0mljc8m8a9twh0g2Vz15LJRMQOgX83SYkO3-N1apmke2Bj9SxFBkvbNUHTBXfz3N-YbIo0gd47izHMROwOkFormLS2nvYBk_g7GMhy7xSjEbpi4p8q3R9XUmWTaAV7d1ze3lcBrz4ugfzIVNeDq44Ce1x3qbhdPRFfZ3n_pNXGn57VXIlkDsHE0QxUu0k-effJgXXeGyc=> . 


Remarketing Thru Email


Not a day goes by that there isn't yet another wrinkle to Facebook ads strategy rippling through the ecosystem. Inside Facebook's Brittany Darwell says targeting-by-email according to its sources and even has a screenshot. Darwell writes, "If this test rolls out to all Power Editor users and the Ads API, companies will be able to remarket to people through News Feed and other Facebook ad units." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OXsacGSihWlKNN8tjlojjDodmq7U_9q-dYjgdnVD4wSshlVvpS8XR3bWJLKh2LygngaHYcBF41aORj4TLflSE5kk6bAINJuOBj-S_KF_MfAzohly7F-7r5HANgLQ9CDhqXgxF7NQSQkv2ICd9b-0ROPpY4LMRQGZ86dtqHgvwozkjRSuB4ZCeuNeP5Gjk3-CqInywR5ASEV_Bwc2WboOlNsLdFqpX-RXZqkUcRhyLyUqBXITfcalFA==>  


Buying Audience, Leaving It Alone


U.S. President Barack Obama's sudden appearance on Reddit last week shined a light once again on the Conde Nast subsidiary. Reaching nearly 20 million uniques monthly, The NY Times David Carr notes that Reddit is still looking for a way to scale revenue. But Conde Nast (owned by Advance) president and Reddit board member Bob Sauerberg isn't worried as he tells Carr, "There will be ample opportunity to monetize what they have built as it grows, and it will be a very big business." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OXsacGSihWkSzLvIJvepoHmfG51TvbuPeGxoeRW050ed1Q0Wi4VdFegC7w1Uq_n7Ma0qTneYEFljvonsSmAoGI6JOmyDqqoNBWfpm_iY81ZjdsiXYm606LKyQOJTZp-vJYBcjLRAG9xwCoErQ2W47aNFhi-x_6bCcdD_7t6c9cqFFwfIeNS__BMlxKbGXwGqVFRctbAj6VFLr5Po8uE7oqbLkblW5kiy10vffyGzwkK0p_-ryqcilw4K9HzW_Bu5wMQO2kU3Z-v7Kh1z71JAcQ==>  Reddit co-founder and board member Alexis Ohanian will speak at AdExchanger's Human Centered Automation conference <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OXsacGSihWkSzLvIJvepoHmfG51TvbuPeGxoeRW050ed1Q0Wi4VdFegC7w1Uq_n7Ma0qTneYEFljvonsSmAoGI6JOmyDqqoNBWfpm_iY81ZjdsiXYm606LKyQOJTZp-vJYBcjLRAG9xwCoErQ2W47aNFhi-x_6bCcdD_7t6c9cqFFwfIeNS__BMlxKbGXwGqVFRctbAj6VFLr5Po8uE7oqbLkblW5kiy10vffyGzwkK0p_-ryqcilw4K9HzW_Bu5wMQO2kU3Z-v7Kh1z71JAcQ==>  in two weeks. 


Right Audience And So On


On his personal blog, marketing pundit Seth Godin appears to be 100% in support of audience buying. After explaining web advertising shortfalls, including "the click" obsession, he writes, "Until advertisers start to value the focused, memorable, impactful opportunity they have in buying the right ads in the right place for the right audience, web users are going to be stuck seeing irrelevant ads on sites that don't respect their time and attention as much as they should." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001OXsacGSihWmCnhYS42Lg3FHZdzcAJLhXRwRHOI6Lu_9CAGD423K7L_hJqrwrh53WY-Ljid5d7dQlkiJ2cOA5smjGsb-PoX9jUBAsy3G4SNY4tbnPE_eGfNf7B24Y-BiRztxWfV-BOzPm3g5lz-GFUbF9AR4eKY6hVtyGXnidUybrihGZv0YbXdtkzu9PzkuIcJ91BE3MY-ZqB-WFYZeITFe6ncWV_5iyhh9bPg_P4oE=>
